Oh, sons, since I have completed this book for you, which is the last part of the science of medicine, by its completion one achieves perfection in it, and through its explanations and declarations, it seems to me that I have provided you with a comprehensive treatise, which is a division of the practical work, namely surgery.
For the practical work is so neglected in our region and in our time, that it has greatly suffered the decline of its science, and its practice is forgotten; and there remain none of it except for a few small descriptions in the books of the Ancients, which were obscure and led to error and confusion, until the understanding of it was obscured and its force was weakened and the art was prolonged.
And it seems to me that I will revive this in the ordering of this treatise, in this way: by explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and so that it comes to the forms of the preparations of cauterization and of other instruments of the work, as is necessary for the addition of the declaration, and for its preparation.
But the reason why no artisan is found with their own art in our time, is that the art of medicine is long and requires its practitioner to be exercised in the science of anatomy, which includes knowledge of the junctions of the members and the forms of those, and the connection and separation of them; and also the recognition of the bones, nerves, and cartilages, and their names, and their relation; and of the pulsating veins and the quiet ones, and the places of their origin.
And according to Hippocrates, the name of this condition is a word, more often used in minor works, and especially in the art of the hand.
We have already spoken of that in the introduction to this book; for whoever is not knowledgeable about what we have said regarding anatomy, it is not surprising that they fall into error by which men die, as has been seen with many of them, because some are formed in this science and turn away from it and lack experience.
For I have seen a foolish and inexperienced doctor having made an incision into a scrofulous aposteme on the neck of a woman, and having cut some arteries of the neck, through which a large amount of blood flowed, until the woman fell dead among her people.
And I saw another doctor who prescribed that he would swallow a stone of a man which was stuck in his throat, and the stone was large, and came out to him and extracted that stone with a piece of the bladder, through which that man on the third day died.
And I have already called it foolish to extract that, and I saw that because of the size of the stone and the condition of the patient, I conjectured that he would die.
And I saw another doctor who received a stipend from a duke of our land for surgery, and he applied to a wretched black man, who had a fracture in his thigh; and with his ignorance, the doctor extracted the fracture, on top of the wound, with poultices and splints with strong structure, and did not leave the wound to heal.
And return the disjointed according to the desires of the sick, and return the relaxed, and return the loosened by walking and commanding that we loosen the ligament; and it is necessary that this be between the thigh and the foot, so that the abscess forms, and turns into a loss.
And it is called a relief to him, and the preparation to loosen the ligament is achieved, and obtained is tranquility and thus alleviation from his pains.
But when corruption had already established itself in the member, because it could not be restrained, and the corruption did not cease to spread in the member until the disease reached a crisis.
And I saw another doctor who made a cancerous abscess, and it was ulcerated in the same days, until the evil of it was magnified with the lord of it, the patient.
This is because the bitter humor is pure melancholy, then it is not suitable that it should penetrate to him entirely, but rather that it should be in a member which suffers so that all of it would be evacuated.
And for this reason, sons, it is necessary for you that the operation on the ill person be divided into two divisions: one is the operation in which health is associated, and the other is the work in which there is danger in the major dispositions.
And you have already examined this in every place of this book where an operation is described in which there is error and fear; for which it is necessary that you guard against this and avoid that, so that the foolish do not find a way to speak and accuse you.
And then take your arms with solicitude and protection from God, and your patients with facility and firmness.
And use the best way by the grace of God to bring about health and praiseworthy success, and leave behind the terrible illnesses of difficult cure, and remove from your arms that which makes you afraid, so that trust in your faith and in your name does not fail you: for greater is the remainder of your glory, and afterwards in the world and lastly among your sanctities.
Certainly I have spoken in some sick men's warnings: “Do not treat the bad illness poorly, so that bad doctors are not named”.
And you have already devoted this book to three chapters.
Begin the division of the book, and first from the first part. The first chapter deals with the head and the feet, in the forms of instruments and in the preparations of cauteries, and with what is necessary for the operation.
The division of the second part. The second chapter, on dryness and perforation, and on ventoses, and on plasters, and on extraction of arrows and on similar things to those, all chaptered and ordered in the forms of instruments.
The third chapter, on restoration and dislocation, and on treatment of twists and on similar things to those; chapter ordered from head to feet, and on the forms of instruments.
When I describe the quality of the juices of that cautery and its outcomes, and in which condition it is prohibited to apply a cautery.
Therefore I say that the discourse on the quality of the juice of cautery and its outcome is a long and prolix discourse, subtle for science, and hidden secret; and already many wise men have spoken about it, and they are discordant among themselves, and for me it suffices to take a little from their discourses, fearing prolixity.
And therefore I say that cautery is suitable for all universal complexion, whatever the material or non-material may be, except for two complexions, which are cold complexions without material.
In the complicated and dry matter, it will be decided; for some said that a cautery is helpful for that, and others said the opposite of that, that a cautery is not convenient in an illness which is due to heat and dryness, because the nature of fire is heat and dryness, and it's convenient that a hot and dry illness with a cautious and dry treatment will be healed.
And they say that which says the opposite of that, that with a cautery is made a remedy for all hot and dry illnesses that occur in the bodies of men, because when you compare the body of man and its humidity to the complexity of fire, you find the body of man is cold.
And I say by the sermon of that one, that I have already experimented this myself many times and discovered.
But I more openly say that it is not necessary for what has already been tried and discussed in the chapter on cauteries through previous exercise, and to have understood the diversity of the complexity of men and the disposition of illnesses in their treatments, and the causes of those, and the accidents of them, and the timing of those.
But in other complications, it is not about your fear, and especially in cold and humid illnesses, because already all doctors are in agreement on those, and they do not disagree on the treatment with a cautery in those.
And you should know, sons, that the secret of cure by cautery with fire and the goodness of it, is that on a medical cautery, the fire is simple, whose action does not penetrate except to the member which is cauterized and does not reach another member of the body except for a small injury.
But the action of medical fire penetrates to that in the members where it is joined, and it makes come to the member with difficulty of healing a strong help and assistance.
But fire, by its subtlety and the goodness of its substance, does not make it exceed except that it is superfluous; And we have joined to us through experiment and through length of service of study in the art on the truth of causes; and for this I excuse the length of the sermon; And if it were not that it is not read in my free will in this passage, a secret hidden with fire, and the quality of its operation in bodies and of its expulsion by which you expel diseases, in a philosophical demonstrative sermon, which would be sharp in your thoughts.
And know, sons, that they disagree about the time in which it is convenient to do a cautery and they pause for the best time of spring.
And I say that cautery is convenient at all times, because the harm caused by the accident in time is submerged in the benefit of what the cautery attracts, and especially if the cautery is for pains or necessary pains, strong and frequent, which do not suffer delay for fear of those that bring malice, which is greater than small harm entering through time.
And also do not step on your feet, or, sons, that they do not esteem except the common people and foolish doctors, it is that for that illness which is healed by cautery there is not need for all time, and they pause to consider the consequences.
And the cause is not known thus by them because of that, for cautery is not but in place of medicine which alters the complexion and dries the humidity which are the cause for which come the pains.
More, I prefer cautery above medicine for the will of its validity and virtue of its operation and greatness of its lord.
And it is possible that the illness returns at some hour of time, according to the complexion of the patient and the location of the illness, and the virtue of it, and that which is prepared in the body from the aggregation of superfluities in it, and that which has come to it through its acquisition of food and similitudes of those causes; except that the illness in which cautery is administered is a subtle illness in a member with few superfluities and humidity, just as a cautery for a tooth for pain and similitude to that, it is possible that in it the pain does not return, but rather decreases.
And most vulgar speech is that cautery is the last resort of medicine, and it is a speech of ignorance, not because they understand it, but because they believe that it is not a cure that is improved by medicine nor by any other cause except for applying cautery.
And the cause is to the contrary; and the intention that cautery is the last resort of medicine is only when we administer the means of cure in certain illnesses, and those medicines do not work, and then at the end of the treatment, cautery is administered, and improved by that. And it is said here that cautery is the last resort of medicine, not according to the intention which is understood by the common people and ignorant doctors.
And the ancients said that cautery with gold is better than cautery with iron, and they did not say this except for the equality of gold and the sublimity of its substance.
And they said that the place of cautery does not matter, as it is not absolutely true, because it has been proven and found that it does not work except in some bodies other than the others, and cautery with gold is good and better than with iron, as they said; but however when you do cautery with fire or with gold, it is not declared to you, because it is done according to the quantity that you want for the roughness of the gold, and prepare to receive cold; and if you adjust it on the ignited spot, the gold melts by the fire, and pour some lamellas into the fire so that the artisan can take it for the occupation of that.
And by this a cautery iron is made with a gentle touch and properly applied to the rectitude of operation.
And I have already ordered this chapter on the cautery according to chapters, and I have ordered those of the head within the feet, so that I alleviate the demanding thing that he wants from it.
The first chapter.
This cauterization is contrary to humidity and cold on the servant's accidental [condition] of which there are two causes, so it is a cause of sweat and multitude of fluxes, called rheumatism, from the head to the parts of the ears and of the hearing fluent, and multitude of sleeping, and of pain in the teeth and of the throat, and universally of all malady that comes from cold, as well as paralytic, and apoplectic, and similar things in those maladies.
The form of this cauterization is this, that first we command the patient to be evacuated with a laxative medicine for three or four nights, according to what the virtue of the malady and their age and their custom require.
And then command him to shave his head with a razor, and then make him sit between your hands on a wooden bench and place your hands on his chest.
And then stop the flow of your palm near the foot on the flow of the nose between the two heels. More precisely, when the vein of the middle place is perforated, mark that place with a probe, and apply the olive cautery, which is the shape of this:
And then stop that on the place you are probing with a hand that presses down, in such a way that the vein is constricted little by little, and you turn it.
And then lift your hand gently and examine the place, and if you see the bone being uncovered to some extent of the head, like the quantity of a grain of barley, then lift your hand, and if it does not return to its previous position, or if another one appears, if it is inflamed, until what has been said to you is seen by the bone.
And then take a little salt and dissolve it on the place and apply it for three days.
And then stop it on the cloth wrapped in cotton and place it on until the scar of the wound is destroyed by the fire. And then heal the place with four-part ointment until it is healthy.
And it has been said that as the wound becomes larger, so much better will be the arm, because it is more improved and younger.
They said that part of it should be cauterized where the bone enters, and hold the cautery in such a way that it touches some portion of the bone's marrow.
And then scrape off what is attached to the bone, and then let it heal.
They said that others with the cautery should reach to the back, so that it presses into the bone strong pressure so that the bone breaks, and this is the method of small aphtha. And they think that from that place come out the vapors of the head.
And let the wound be kept open for a long time, and then be treated until it is consolidated.
But to me, these two species of cautery have not been seen, except in some men according to the way of fear; and it seems to me, better is health, when it is; for the head is revealed by solution of continuity of the aforementioned, as we have testified in other members, and especially when the head of the patient is of frail nature.
And the first species of cautery is safer and better, in my opinion; and from that practice and with that work comes health.
Chapter according to.
Of the cautery of the head.
When the head suffers from chronic and prolonged pain, and this is in the patient's prolonged illness, and uses treatments such as poultices and suppositories and head wraps and plasters and bandages and cold compresses and liniments and remedies, and especially if it has already been cauterized with a cautery that has not relieved the symptoms of those causes, then consider whether the patient's head is of strong constitution in its nature; and it is not fragile and suffers from great cold, then that cautery should be done with another cautery, leaving the previous one. Then cauterize that area on the horn of the sick head with a cautery until the cord is severed. Cut the cord and expose the bone the amount that we have described, and cauterize it with a cautery in the right part of the head, in the place which is called "vas" — and this is the place where airy flesh is found. And lift your hand thus, and do not expose the bone, because the patient suffers from very great pain different from the pain of all the other head cauteries.
And I say that this cautery in its place, because it is known that the cautery with which the horns of the head and the occiput are cauterized is a more subtle cautery than the one with which the middle part of the head is cauterized; and this is the form of it.
Head of the bed.
From the cauterization of an old migration.

And then apply a bandage over the wound with a tight compression, and leave it there for three hours; and then undo it and treat the salt, and leave the poultice on for two or three days, and apply a plaster submerged in hot water until the place forms a scab.

And if you want, make this with some burning medicines which have been written about in the second treatise on burning medicines.

Chapter five.
On the cauterization of ear pains.
When in the ear there is pain from cold and it is treated with lacative causes and with the other cure that has been spoken of in the division, and the pain is not relieved, then ignite the cautery, and this is what is called a point, of which this is the form:
And apply the point near the ignition, and let it be carried around the entire ear as if a wheel is turned, or in a circle around each part if the pain is in each part. Bring yourself to the cautery of the root of the ear little by little until you feel the place with your finger.
And if the cautery of ten points on the entire ear, and cauterize it, then treat the places until they are healed.
Chapter six.
On the cauterization of torture.
Torture that is cured with cauterization is not one of the species that come from flow, as we have said in the divisions of illnesses.
Avoid cauterization of the species that originates from dryness or from spasm of the nerve.
When you cure that species of torture with poultices and capers and gargling, and you do not confirm your cure, then it is known that you should cauterize the illness with three cauterizations: give one to the root of the ear, and a second a little below the temple, and the third give to the junction of the two lips.
And place the cauterization on the opposite side of the affected part, because mollification is only seen in the part that appears to be healthy.
And the form of cauterization is that you cauterize it with the cauter on the right side of the extremity of the ear, a little above the horn of the head, and in the temple another, the length of which should be according to the length of the aforementioned finger, and put your hand with the cauter inside until the quantity of the matter of the species of the cod is consumed.
And this is the shape of the cautery, and it is a species of the knife, the shape of which is in front of the table. More subtle is that which takes away a little, as it seems to me; and I believe that cutting from the superfluous fatness a little.
And then heal the place with what is in front, processed within so that it may be healthy.

And the handling of the cautery is done according to what has been previously said.
And it is cauterized above the mouth of the stomach; and it is more dangerous; and then it is treated with what is processed.

Chapter ten.
On the cauterization of epilepsy.
It is not the epileptic who should be cauterized, but that the epilepsy is due to a flux.
And therefore we advise that you modify the brain of the patient at the beginning with a mixture and another cure, which we have dictated in the division when the illness is great and it tolerates the exception of medicines.
And if it is a child who cannot tolerate medicines, then administer gargling treatments and masticators to the servant that modifies, giving that for many days, with improvement of the food.
And return to the head of the patient, and then cauterize that one with a cautery in the middle place of the head according to the preceding manner, and with another cautery on the occiput of it, and on each horn of the head let it be cauterized. And if the patient is strong and tolerant, then cauterize them with the same cautery that has been mentioned, having previously softened and loosened the body on the vertebrae of the neck and the vertebrae of the back.
And let the olive oil be cauterized according to what has been stated previously.
But if the patient is a child, then apply a subtle cautery in this manner.
Chapter 11.
On the cauterization of melancholy.

And shave the head of the patient, and make a decently made plaster of egg on the circle, and apply it to the middle place of the head.
And let the patient be sitting upright, and let them be held firmly from all sides.
And apply a liniment; it is also worthy to anoint the eyelids with elderberry. Heat that one on the fire with tempered warmth by measure, which the said sufferer feels most in it. And apply that to the middle place of the head of it in a circle, and release it within so that it is refreshed.
Make that to the patient for a whole week, with another regimen of it inside until it is healed; or if you wish, cauterize that making small points according to the size of it, provided you hold the hand with a cautery thus ordered: this is a type of cautery which moistens the brain with equality.
And then put that cut in a poultice or in wraps of gualina.
Chapter twelve.

Chapter sixteen.
Of the cautery of the eyelid of the eye when the skin is converted to the inner parts and the eye is punctured.
When the skin of the eye is converted to the inner parts so that it punctures the eye, then cautery is done in two ways, either with iron or with medicinal applications.
If you apply the cautery with fire to the patient, command them beforehand that they should lift their skin like those who are about to be treated, until they are lengthened and widened; and if the needle is piercing too deeply, then tie the eyes of the patient with a bandage so that it is not moved until the skin is grown.
Then when they are grown and widened, place the head of the patient on your thigh, and apply a sign above the eyelid of their eyes with a thread, which is shaped like a fig leaf, and let this signal be close to the skin.
And then stop putting cotton in the wound or in the poultice of pitch on the ulcer.
And then apply the cautery of which this is the shape.
And then cauterize on the figure that has been designed, little by little, in small burned spots, until the surface of the quiver is completely burnt, which appears like a fig tree leaf, clearly apparent.
Signal of sanity of the present work is that you see the eyelid of the eye already being contracted and the skin of it being elevated due to the puncture of the eye.
And then raise your hand and leave it there for three days, and then put on the wound a bandage until the scar is formed. And then heal that with an ointment until it is healed.
But if it returns through the skin for some reason, then apply another treatment and the eyelid is softened, then do another time the cautery on that one just as you had done previously.
But if the skin grows on the eyelid, then cauterize it until it is elevated to its own natural place and is evened out so that the skin does not touch the eye.
Put the cautery in medicine to burn and this is what commands the patient to raise their skin while they are prolonged and narrowed, and then make a paper of cloth in the shape of a miter's funnel.
And then take soap made from congealed and living snake, or what is called aqua, and mix those things together, and make a paste to prevent it from being cold; and then spread that paste on the paper which is made in the shape of a miter's funnel, and apply that to one of the soles of the feet; and apply the heel wrapped in a poultice of warm water, and let the patient's head be in a raised position.
And then put the finger on the medicine and press it a little and not on the veins so that the patient feels the biting of the medicine, because this biting is in him like fire.
And then when he perceives that the medicine has a biting sensation, then raise the medicine and put it on the upper finger; then when the biting stops, then remove the medicine and wash the heel with water; and then consider if the swelling is already lifted like something washed of constriction by fire or incision, because this is good; and if it does not return to that place where the medicine was applied and does not diminish until the operation is completed and the heel is contracted.
And then pause on the patient's back to ensure that the stiffness of the adjustment is eradicated, and treat that area with a soothing ointment or another entrance so that it may be healed.
And it is necessary for you, that you must guard your operation with vigilant diligence so that no part of the medicine falls into the eye, and if the eyelid is softened in some days and some cause of the skin pinches in the eye, then apply your medicine to that area where the eyelid is softened, and properly as it was done at the beginning, and apply a dressing to ensure that it may be healed.
And this is the form of application of the plaster.
And you should know that the eyes of men are diversified according to size and smallness, and thus your contraction is made accordingly.
And let not be hidden the way of rectitude to he who has studied in this art.
Chapter 18.
Of cauterization of the fistula that is in the tear duct of the eye.
When you treat a fistula with the method that we have discussed in the divisions of illnesses and do not confirm your treatment, then it is necessary that you cauterize it in this manner: command the patient to pause with their head held back, and hold the head of the patient by some servant between the hands in such a way that it may not be moved nor agitated with the head.

When the throat is treated with blood in the way that we have spoken of in the division of the cure with medicines and not with confectures, then consider the throat of the patient to the sun, since you have comprehended the tongue of them with an instrument which you have recommended.
Therefore, if you see the blood, extract it with a small pinch or with subtle and decent gestures.
And if it is not possible for you to extract it, then take a concave cannula and insert it into the throat of the patient, and place in the cavity of the cannula an ignited iron, and do this as many times (until the blood is stopped and removed from the throat) and abstain the patient from water for the whole day.
And then take a full pitcher of cold water, and put the patient's mouth in it, and wash their mouth with it; and do not swallow any of this water for any reason, but rather spit out the water an hour after, because as soon as the blood senses the cold water.
More often if the patient is not previously prepared with what we have recommended, then subject the patient to steam or to a poultice made with the instrument that we have recommended in the steaming of the palate.
Make that, which is in four courses.
And there is another manner of operation in the steaming of that, which you take a bowl in which are ignited coals and the bowl is covered with a cover in the middle of which is a hole, and let the extremity of the instrument be composed in that hole; and apply it from below to the steam; and put the patient's mouth on the extremity of the pipe, and close their mouth so that the steam is not wasted until you know that the steam has reached the blood, because the blood as much flows.
And if it doesn't work, then repeat the steaming many times, and abstain the patient from drinking, and make them eat salty and bitter foods, and don't drink water, and it is necessary that with this regimen the patient be prepared.
And this is the form of the instrument with which the blood of the throat is treated when it is seen; and it resembles a forceps as many times, except that it is in some curvature: The one that is placed on the pillow, and the extremity of it resembles a beak of a cicada, which is a gouty tumor, in which there is an accumulation of lime, for this reason, when we press upon some cause, that one does not let go.
Chapter 40.
In which there is the sum of the serum in perception of abscesses and in section of their discharge.
The abscesses show special symptoms, of various kinds, according to what we recall about them, each one in this book.
And they are diverse in perforation and discharge of them through two methods, of which one is for the species of abscesses in themselves being treated; and for that which we comprehend of the humidities.
And the second method is proper for the places in which accidents of the body occur, because the abscess that happens in the head is different from the abscess that happens in the buttocks; and the abscess in a fleshy place is different from the abscess in a joint; and each one of them is judged by operation.
And among abscesses there are some which it is advisable that they not be perforated but rather waiting for the maturation of the blood in them or the completion of it.
Other abscesses that are formed when they are pierced, and not matured according to their nature, like abscesses that are applied to the joints, because an abscess is applied to a joint, its substance is prolonged until it has consumed what is in its circuit, and it has corrupted the ligaments or nerves of that joint, for which it is made cause of contraction of that member; or it is an abscess proper to a principal member, and if you delay the perforation of it until it is matured, it will harm the principal member; or it is proper to the anus, therefore perforate what is not matured; and it is not necessary to perforate the crude, of undigested digestion, but that which is proper to the anus, so that it does not press on its bottom and is elongated to the inner parts of the anus, and a fistula is made, or that which is made in the term of it which is not sanitized. It is necessary that you know the time of the perforation of the abscess, and also when it is matured.
And you will know that it is matured when there is a reduction of the pain and a cessation of the fever, and also a decrease in swelling and pulsation, and a sharpening of the head of the abscess, and other signs.
And where it is necessary that you know the perforation cauterizes in the place of the abscess and of the pus coming from the treatment of the prominent area.
And the cauterization is done through the depth of the flesh or body, if the abscesses are in the parts of the hands or feet, and in the place of the arteries, of the nerve cords, of the tendons; and, finally, in all hidden places where there is no reflection; for in those that are reflected, use cauterization according to that member.
But when the abscess is in a fleshy place, it is better that you delay the cauterization until digestion is confirmed according to the compliment, as we have said; for if you cauterize it at that time, it prolongs the body of the pus and increases its foulness, and forces out the lips of the wound which become hardened and increases the depth of it.
But some abscesses are cauterized according to the thickness of the flesh or body depending on necessity, or according to that which the affected member indicates.
And it is necessary that you administer small cauterization, and in large abscesses a large and wide cauterization or several incisions according to the diversity of the size of the abscesses.
And other symptoms of the abscesses in which it is believed that the gland is affected and inflamed, when it is made thus with bread and made in term that it already starts to suppurate, just like that which occurs in cases of swelling and boils.
And of those that are incised with a section having three angles; and of those it is in which is incised thus as the figure of a leaf of mint, thus as the abscesses of the glands.
And of them in which is administered a round section and a crescent-shaped section, similar to those.
More, that one which does not fit thus as are abscesses, being superficial, it is believed that you should puncture it with a superficial puncture, or just flatten it.
And it is believed that when the abscess is large and has collected much pus, that you should puncture it and not be concerned that you extract all the pus at that hour; having extracted a portion from it, and then apply a poultice to the abscess until the next day, and then extract a larger portion, and then do this several times according to the gradual process until it is completely evacuated.
And especially if the patient is of fragile virtue, or a pregnant woman, or a small child, or an old person in decline, because the animal spirit is resolved with the evacuation of the pus, and for this reason it dies, and you operate on them.
Keep this chapter with great caution, and approach your perforation in which you make these apostems, considering that you clean the wounds and see if the wound of the apostem is small, or is a flat section, then you administer poultices of lime or of hot cinders; and if the apostem is large, and the fissures of the perforation are many, then consider that you apply a plaster on each hole so that they heal together.
And if in the apostem a part of the skin is cut off or has been hollowed out in the circuit, then consider that you fill it with hot cloth or with yarn made from linen thread, as when you treat ulcers or wounds, its humidity; and bind it for three days; and approach the process and cure it with what is necessary to anoint until it is healed.
Moreover if a flow of blood occurs at the time of your operation, then you administer cold water and vinegar in the places where you apply a linen cloth, and place it over the area of the abundant and visible bleeding.
Moreover if the flow of blood persists, then consider that you administer treatment and cure with powders which have been recommended in many places of this our book and division.
More often if it is in winter time, and the place of the abscess is a place of nervous motion, then you should apply poultices of warm oil and cauterized wool, and put them on the affected areas.
And if it is in summer, and the areas are fleshy, then you should apply poultices soaked in water and oil or in warm wine and oil, and all this should be applied with friction for three days, as we have said, and then you should open the abscess and clean it and administer the treatment that is suitable for the patient.
And this is what is necessary for the knowledge of the treatment of abscesses in general, but according to the method of distinction I have already spoken of all abscesses in which manner the way of cure is by chapters singularly.

Chapter twelve.
Of the section of the species of knots.
Of the knots, some species and I have already said all the species of them in the division.
And I will show you the difference between a knot and an abscess with a clear explanation.
Therefore I say that with an abscess there is heat and fever and vehement pains until the ebullition of the surplus is sedated; and it is a completed putrefaction which then stops the fever, pain, and heat.
But with a knot there is no heat nor fever nor pain, and it contains that hip or hernia which is in its own sack.
And it is according to the color of the body, and its beginning is like a cyst and is made thus as a vacuity, whether major or minor, and they are according to two species, which are either fat or contain humidity, and the colors of the humidity are many, as I have said in the division.
Therefore I say, when you approach the cure of a knot, that you explore and inquire into its beginning with the instrument which is called an introducer, according to how its shape will be found in the chapter which is appropriate for this.
It is the technique of inquiring about abscesses and all nodes, and it is that you take this instrument and insert it into the place where you find humidity in the abscess, and you will turn the thumbs of the patient little by little so that you know that the instrument has already penetrated the abscess.
And then put your hand according to the size of the abscess, and extract the inserted part and consider what comes out from the remains of it.
And if the running humidity is forgotten, of whatever color it may be, then you will cut it with a superficial incision according to what has been said about other abscesses.
And if from the remains of the insertion there is no humidity, then you will know that it is a fatty tissue.
And cut above it with an incision having the shape of a cross according to this shape: thus as you have been taught, and suspend that with a hook, and scratch the abscess from all parts with ease, and if possible, place a dressing or bandage over it, and extract that liquid from the knot.
But if it breaks during the operation, it is not possible to extract that liquid, and you will see bits of tissue coming out, and then you will extract it with tweezers until none of it remains.
If of the fluid a small or excessive amount, the knot returns according to the size.
And if you see that a small part of the fluid is retained, then complete the wound with some sharp corrosive powders and tighten the wound, and place a cauterized plaster on it, and cure that which needs another internal treatment until it is healed.
And if the knot is large, then sew the two lips of it and cure it with that which will make it heal together.
Mostly if the pulse is at the opposite, or not pulsing, then touch and fill the place of the third vein that is varnished and apply a tight bandage for two days or three until the wound closes and the swelling of the blood subsides; and then return to separate that which is the matter of the knot.

And it is known in the science of midwifery that a strong woman aids in that labor with a similar device, and thus one operates on it as if it were a womb.
Chapter 76.
Of the extraction of the dead fetus.
When you treat a dead fetus with the method we have mentioned in the division of medicine and it is not forced out, and you are not skilled in using the operation with your hands, then consider if the woman is of good virtue and not at risk of accidents for which loss on her part is feared.
Then it is that the woman should be placed on her back on a seat or bed, and her head should be inclined downwards and her thighs elevated.
And the assistant should hold the two parts of her, or tie her to the seat, so that her body does not move away from the extraction of the fetus.
And then anoint the mother's mouth with olive oil and mucus of altaea and of fenugreek and of sesame seed.
And then the midwife anoints her hand with those oils and mucus, and then inserts her hand with ease into the mother, and then seeks with her hand the place where the fetus is stuck.
And find a convenient place for this: then consider if the foot is prepared to be placed on the head, and then put the ankles in the heels of it, or in the neck, or in the mouth, or in the palate, or leave the beard, or in the furrow of it, or in the proper places of the ribs, or leave the hypochondriums.
More if the placement is on the feet of it, then in the penis, or in the middle of the ribs.
And take the ankle with the right hand, and hold the curvature of it in that place which is between the fingers of the left hand, and insert the hand with ease and put the ankle in some of those places we have mentioned, until you reach the underlying cause.
Then take and place on the opposite side of it another ankle, or the thigh if necessary, so that it is attracted equally, and not extended according to its natural straightness alone.
And massage the entire affected area, so that its discomfort is alleviated just as it is done in order to eradicate it.
And take in that which is between them that the extension should be softened; and if any part of it is retained, then take that the midwife anoints some of her fingers with oil and inserts them gently and stirs with those fingers the retained area.
Therefore, if the part of the foot is dislocated, then the ankles are loosened and placed in the area where it should be; and do so until the entire foot is dislocated.
But if the hand is displaced outward from the other, and it's not possible to reduce it by constraining it, then take a cloth that has been wrapped around it; and carefully extract it until it's entirely dislocated, and reset it either in the joint of the hand or in the elbow.
And do the same on the other hand and on both feet.
But if the head of the foot is large, or is constricted in the swelling, or is in the head of the water being adjusted, then take a spatula and insert it between the tendons and split the head and extract the water, or that it be scraped with an instrument which is called “alundat”, the shape of which will be described along with the shapes of other instruments in the chapter which is relevant to this.
And similarly do if the foot has a large head by nature: then take and reset it with a chisel, or that it be scraped with an alundat as we have said; and carefully extract the bones with the forceps.
And if the head is elevated and constricted by the pillow, then it should be cut out so that the humidity which is in the chest is evacuated.
More or less, if it's not complicated, nor an obstruction to elevation, then you will incline the head as much as is possible to you.
And if the abdomen is swollen with an abscess or it is dropsical, then it is necessary that you perforate that area so that the humidity which is in it can flow out.
More or less, if the fetor is above the two feet, then the attraction of it is lighter and the direction of it to the mouth of the matrix is lighter.
More or less, if it is constricted by the abdomen and chest, then it is necessary that you extract that which you have wrapped with a cloth over your hand, and that you cut the abdomen and chest so that what is in them can flow out.
More or less, if the other members are stopped and the head is turned, then the left hand enters; more or less, if the mouth of the matrix is opened, then the hand enters the womb, and near that, the head is turned, and it attracts that with the fingers into the mouth of the matrix, and places one or two fingers inside, and pulls it towards those.
And if the mouth of the womb is constricted by an apostemal cautery which adheres to it, then beware that it does not cause turmoil within it; however, beware then to administer an infusion of humid and fatty substances. Then administer plasters; and follow the patient with waters that soften and moisten.
And if the pain is on the side of the liver, then if possible, it should be pricked: and there should be administered what we have said for the painful liver.
And if that is not possible, then let it be cut into pieces, and extracted.
And beware that you do not leave any cause of pain within the second intestine.
And when you have completed all your operation, then administer what we have said about the cure of apostems, those that adhere to the womb.
And if there is an adherence of bloody flux, then dip in astringent waters and administer the other cure.
And I have already seen a woman in whose womb the fetus was dead, and then upon that place another conceived fetus, and then the dead fetus is another matter. It adheres to the navel for a long time an apostem; and it is inflated between the womb and the intestines, and begins to throw out arms.
And you were called to treat him, and you treated him for a long time, but the wound is not consolidated.
Then you applied to him from some causes a plaster of strong attraction, and extracted from him a bone, and then passed the urine, and extracted another bone; and you were very marvelled, since there is no bone in the belly.
And then you thought that they were bones of a dead fetus.
Then you probed the wound, and extracted from it many bones, the woman existing in her seventh month of pregnancy, and already had been in such a manner for a long time, and delivered from it a small arm.
And you do not find it strange, but rather that in this there is knowledge and help for that which the doctor's skillful hand administers for the cure.
Of the forms of the instruments that are necessary to extract the fetus.
Form of a vertex with which the mother is opened:
This is the form of a holder in which the limbs are held, to whose holding belong two vertices at the two extremities of two fetuses. It is recommended that this vertex be made more subtle by the craftsman, and that it be made of ivory or of boxwood.
And the width of each thigh is two fingers and the margin of each thigh is one finger, and the length of each thigh is one and a half palms; and in the middle location of two thighs there are two adjustments of that same thigh, which are already firm, of which the length is a little more than half a palm, and the width of each thigh is two fingers or a little less.
And these two additions should be introduced into the mouth of the matrix so that it opens with those when you apply the two prescribed virtues.
Make another similar to that one, but more subtle and lighter:
Let it be made from the fibers of elder or boxwood, according to the resemblance of strengths. More often on the extremity of it put two additions thus times, and the length of these additions is about one palm, and the width of each is two fingers.
And when you want to open the matrix, then make the woman sit on a chair with her feet hanging, opening what is between her thighs. And then take your hand with the instrument thus as you make a hole according to the quantity that you want of the width of the mouth of the matrix, until the thread makes what you want.

Of the extraction of the second [or possibly "the afterbirth" or "placenta"], however considering
When the afterbirth is retained from the birth, then it is necessary that you command the ill woman to retain her seat, and make her vomit with a concoction, and hold your hand over her mouth and over her nostrils, and if by this way she is not discharged, it is good.
And if not, then take a woolen cloth and perforate in the blanket a hole and put in that opened mouth of the mother, thus with warmth and rough and nettle and chamomile and dried Arabic and Cassia wood and holy tree. Soak all these herbs or some of them in water in the cloth, and put that on the womb.
Then put a tube of cane in the mouth of the mother, and hold it until the vapor comes to the cavity of the mother.
And make her vomit in the way we have said, and the afterbirth will be expelled with speed.
But if this cure is not effective, then you command the midwife to insert her left hand into oil of juniper or in a mixture of nutmeg, and then introduce it into the womb and search for the afterbirth, and when she has found it, then take it out little by little. But if it is attached to the womb of the mother, then introduce the hand as we have recommended, and when she has found the afterbirth, extract it slowly so that the mother does not feel vehement pain. Let both sides of the costal areas be permeated with gentle ease on the right and left.
And if the mouth of the matrix is constricted, we have already recommended the cure with purging and medication of the bile with herbs.
But if it is not forgotten with all the causes that we have recommended, then beware that you do not make an iteration of abstraction on that, but rather it is necessary that what comes out of it from the mouth of the matrix to the thigh of the woman, and then apply a plaster and tetra-pharmakon; because that will make her purify for several days and it will be dissolved and forgotten.
But when it is purified, the evil humor is elevated from her to the head and to the stomach, and that oppresses the patient; and then it is necessary that sub-phumigations and conveniences be administered to her.
But some of the Ancients already used a sub-phumigation of dried nasal snuff and of dried figs.
Shape of an instrument with which the woman is fumigated to retain the menses and the secondine ( likely referring to a device used to treat female disorders, such as retention of menstrual flow or afterbirth).
It must be done with sight or by feeling.
And let the thin extremity be placed in the bowl and the wider extremity over the focus, and the sub-fumigation be placed on the arms of the focus.
And hold that one until the sub-fumigation is consumed and another one is put in its place.
Of the treatment of the navel of the unperforated child.
Many children are born and their navels are not perforated, which have a thin and closed cicatrix. Then tell the midwife to pierce that cicatrix with her finger; and if not, pierce it with a sharp spatulum, and be careful not to touch the liver.
And immediately apply on that place a flannel soaked in wine and oil; and treat it with an ointment until it is healed.
But if you fear that it is closed, then put a cannula in the navel for many days, and remove it when the child is able to defecate.
And if there is closure of the navel due to consolidation of a wound or an abscess; then tell that this consolidation should be incised, and immediately treated with what we have said about the treatment and the poultice.
Of the treatment of fistulas that appear in the eyes.
The fistulas that appear in the low part of the eyes are a sign of thickening and nodules, which appear near the anus or in the space of one side.
And it is a fistula or many boils.
And when that nodulation is ancient and corrupted by damp whitish or subtle purulence, and some veins are seen coming from these fistulas, some penetrate.
And those penetrating are known by the fact that a discharge is issued from them through excretion and flatulence; and some times it happens that the patient has diarrhea, and often the worm is expelled from them.
And some of these fistulas are seen in the space penetrating into the bladder, and into the marrow of the penis; and some of these penetrating go into the joint of the thigh and into the knot of the hip.
And that in which a penetrating fistula is recognized as entering into the anus and not entering, is that you put your finger inside the anus, and you insert a thin probe of iron or wire into the fistula when there is no obstruction.
But if there is an obstruction in it, then insert a thin probe of lead or horsehair into which you feel the probe or the hair in your finger.
And if you do not feel anything in the entire abdomen nor any protrusion of the bowel or any cause of evacuation or worms or gas, as we have said, then know that it is non-penetrating, and then touch the area to be treated.
When the fistula is penetrating into the bladder or into the flesh of the penis, then the sign of it is excessive urine from that and prohibition to him from going to the place where medicine will be applied to consolidate it.
More so if it is penetrating into the joint of the thigh or into the bone and increases pain in the circle, then the signal of it is that the tenderness is felt inside here, if there is not brittleness inside the bone, and increase of pain in the circuit of the affected part; and that of it produces pus and discharge; and that it does not respond to medication, nor is consolidated with ointment.
And in all those penetrating fistulas there is no cure at all, and the treatment of those is labor and vanity of the foolish doctors, on which they are firm.
But in the one that is not penetrating and not chronic, healing with iron is hoped for, according to what you have recounted, and that which has already been tried and proved.
And it is that the patient lies between your hands on the back of the bed and lifts their legs inside, the thighs are inclined towards their belly, and then insert a probe of lead, or of iron if it's an anal fistula, until you feel the place where the probe penetrates.
And if that sensation causes the patient to turn around the neck, then it is necessary that you insert your finger inside the neck.
And if you feel with your finger that the probe has already penetrated and uncovered the passage, or if you feel between the finger and the sphincter or flesh, then you are certain that it is penetrating; and therefore do not work on that, because it is not in that place where healing will occur, as we have said.
More importantly, I have said to some that certain illnesses are healthy in certain men badly.
And of the medication for which it is hoped that youth is regained in him, it is that you apply subtle cauterization according to the width of the fistula, as previously described, and insert that ignited thing into the fistula until it reaches around the neck; and then repeat this two or three times until you feel that all those adjusted tissues, which resemble a nest of feathers, are adjusted.
And then treat that with warm poultices enveloped in cloth so that all those adhering tissues are softened, and treat that with medicine that engenders and consolidates the flesh, and if it is healed, well; and if not, then it is not healthy within a certain time for another treatment.
And if the probe enters, and does not penetrate through the tissue where it is in the anus, and between that and the probe which is only a few inches of flesh or intestine, and it touches the fistula on what is the surface of the bowel, then cut the bowel from the start of the fistula, and you will cut with the probe, and let it be in the fistula so that the cutting reaches the place where the end of the probe appears, and through the probe it is liberated and emptied.
And then clean those fistulated tissues which are gathered like a tube of straw and not broken by any of these causes.
More often if there is a flow of blood that comes between you and your operation when you dissect those tissues, then the instrument that should be cauterized with fire or with sharp medicine, for cautery with fire adjusts good habits: it is the adjustment of those tissues, and the removal of bad blood, the excision of humidity.
And then treat the wound with warm compresses or trusses applied to the affected area, and also treat the plague with a plaster made from hard fat that generates and consolidates.
And these are the medicines in which there is purging and evacuation; when the treatment is restored, it is already healed and you do not fear relapse.
More often if the fistula has passed into the anus and is extended from the surface of the body, then insert the pointed instrument into the anus and investigate with it.
And therefore if you feel the tension and between you and it is a vein of blood or flesh, and it is prone to penetration, then it is not an operation on it but rather a way of trust and hope.
This cause is to be administered in one of three ways: either that you cauterize the area as we have said; or that you evacuate it by entering and achieving its cavity, so that you can introduce the instruments and the cure provided; and do not proceed with too much evacuation so that you do not irritate the lacert containing the intestine, and that you act on the patient's will and consent; and then treat it with what we have said before, which will strongly heal it; or that you extend the vein and remove the pus that you evacuate from the area near the anus, as we have said, either with a tent or another sharp instrument, and then cleanse the fistulized flesh which is in the evacuated area where you can make an incision; and then strive to make the restoration of the entire wound with evacuation, and if the purulent pus does not consolidate, and the fistula remains open in the part of the anus, it will be easier for the patient. And some fistulas are finished in this manner: it is when you insert the thread into the fistula, and it is in the flesh of the buttocks around the surface of the body with the codena and in the margin of the buttocks, then take the thread of the perforated extremity, which is like a needle for preparing the orifices according to this form:
and insert it into that vein wrapped with 5 veins or around those; and then insert the thread into the vein in the fistula until you achieve the cavity of it.
More if it is penetrating in the margin of the buttocks deeply, then you extract the vein from that hole like you insert your finger in the buttocks; and extract the extremity of the vein and adjust the two extremities together, and tighten each one, and leave it for a day or for two, and when you see the vein coming out of the flesh, tighten until those flesh are coming out which are between the two extremities of the vein and that fall.
And then cure the wound until it is consolidated and healed.
More if the orifice of the fistula does not penetrate, then make it penetrate, in whatever way you have prepared, but that it be more in the groin, because it is not for you to do this so that the urine does not come out; and then do it in such a way that it is healed.
The shape of the spine is where the fistula is split: the curvature of which is very sharp and the other part is not sharp, so that it does not cut unnecessarily, thus as needed.
Of the stitching of swollen veins in which blood runs in the incision of those.
Swollen veins are judged by two methods, whether they are between the hemorrhoids and the buttocks or if they are with a fat of excessive flesh. And of those that are small and large, and where the blood flows from them in abundance, and it is one, and very abundant, and outside the buttocks, and in the extremities of it.
Worse are the ones that are outside the buttocks according to the amount of little humidity, from which flows yellowish water or a small amount of blood with continuous flow, and according to the color of the body.
And the cure of that which is next to the anus is that we command the patient to sit and to strain themselves so that the anus opens and the swollen veins appear to you. Then you touch and lift with your fingers or that you hold them with your nail, and then cut those according to their roots.
If the ulcers are not held in those places due to their humidity and softening, then take those with a coarse cloth or with a cotton swab or with a flannel of wool, and extract those with the fingers, and immediately sprinkle those and powder over them certain powders suitable for the wound, for application instead of cauterization; or cauterize those as previously described in the chapter on cauterization. And then heal those with another cure until they are healed.
And if the anus does not obey the evacuation, then anoint the patient with an ointment in which there is a mild biting, and let it be washed with that water which is in the basin and which will facilitate evacuation gently when the patient presses.
If the hemorrhoids are protruding from the anus, then their cause is alleviated, and it is that you take those with your nail, or that you take those with a needle, and prick them, and immediately heal them with the water that we have mentioned until they are healed.
And for the one who has undergone incision, it is necessary to administer suture in this manner: take thread and insert it into the needle, and then extract the hemorrhoids from the divided parts, and make that penetrate with the needle into the root of the other part, and wrap the two extracted ends of the thread around the divided part below the needle, and lengthwise; and tighten the hemorrhoid with strong stitching, and immediately knot the thread and extract the needle.
Make a cut in that area, and take out one of them, and do not cauterize, so that the excess blood from that wound does not flow.
Then put a poultice on the buttocks made with rose oil or wax; and apply that to the anus, and instruct the patient to rest. And then remove that which falls into a box; and when it is cut, treat those wounds with an ointment or another cure so that they are healed.
And if they are old and not valid in that medicine, then it is advisable to apply those to the point of spit or with your nail so that they are made humid and the pus is drawn out from them, which prohibits their consolidation; and then treat those so that they are consolidated.
Then apply those with a violent purging so that the first thing is blood and they are scraped; and then treat those so that they are healed.
It is known that hemorrhoids, it is clear, and not if there isn't a notable swelling according to the color of the body resembling a head of lavender, and it is made in all the body and mainly in the lower parts near the feet and the thighs, and it comes from those painful veins.
And then it is necessary that what has grown in the area of the groin be held with tongs or with an onion, and be eradicated from its root; and then treat that area.
And if you want, cauterize the second one that is described in the following chapter.
Warts are a small, rough, round, ulcerated protrusion on the surface of the body, and similar growths appear on the hands of children.
And the treatment for it is to stretch and cut that, or to tighten it with a string or a hair that fits into the wound. And if you want, cauterize that, as we have said, with a hot iron or with sharp medicine.
Warts are a small, fatty, ulcerated or fistulous growth on the surface of the body, especially on the thumb, and when you touch it, it seems to be centered in the likeness of a boil, and it is found around the body.
And the treatment for it is to take a needle of cotton thread or of wool thread, and make it strong, and place it over the wart until it is held by the circle of the thread of the parts of it; and then rotate your hand with the needle so that you cut what is in the area of the wart, and press it into the thumb of the flesh, and eradicate the wart from its root.
And if you want, make that with a cane of iron or of wood according to this form:

And if you want, cauterize the woman according to what is stated above in the cauterization of the thigh in the chapter on cauterization.

Of the treatment of wounds.
I have already spoken in the division of the treatment of wounds what is suitable for the free man, and I will speak thus the treatment of those with illness and with medicines according to the complement.
Therefore, I say that wounds are diversified according to what they are made of and according to the place where the wounds occur.
And the causes by which many wounds are made are like gathering of gravel, or cutting with a sword, or with a knife, or beating with a lance, or with a fist, or with an arrow, or similar to those of many other causes.
More wounds that are in the places of the body are like a wound which falls on the head, or the neck, or the chest, or the abdomen, or the liver, and similar to those of the limbs.
And thus we recommend the cure of certain wounds for which we pause this reasoning and rule over other wounds.
And we will begin with the simple head wounds, for the discussion of the composite ones will come after the third chapter.
Therefore, I say that when a simple wound occurs on the head and it's not a fracture, then consider: if it's due to a blow from a stone or something similar, and the skin has been torn only slightly and it's a large wound and you fear the onset of an abscessing caut, then seize the moment and perform a cephalic bloodletting as soon as possible, and don't delay; and extract from that vein according to the quantity of the virtue of it, if there's no prohibitive cause for bloodletting, especially if the blood that comes out of the wound is scarce.
And let the bloodletting be on the opposite side of the wounded part; and protect the patient from replenishment and wine and coarse foods.
But if the condition prohibits any kind of nourishment, then let it be diminished from food and not approached with meat nor wine.
And apply to the wound, if an abscessing caut occurs to it, cotton soaked in rose oil or in wine where it has been steeped.
More is it certain of the postrema cauter, then pause over the wound, if it is recent with blood and the air has not changed that powder which you will recommend to apply little by little.
And if the air has already changed it, then pause on the healing ointments until it is healed.
But if the wound is large or is by incision of flesh and of similar things, and the lips of it are not adjusted for stitches, then adjust them with a suture as you will recommend from the suture of others.
But if the wound has already exposed the bone and flesh, and it is not retained by them but only a small suspensor, then incise that and apply cure to the wound with medicines and restore the flesh in place of putridness, and command the patient to abstain from foods in which there is grossness: cabbage and beans and similar things to them, until it is composed.
And if you find in the wound putrid rottenness and it does not adhere to the bone, then cut away all that rotten part and throw it away, and apply cure to it.
But if in these wounds there is an artery or vein from which a flow of blood can come, and it is not stopped by medicines, then inquire about the artery, and if you find it uncut, then cut it with a spatula, or tie it; and if necessity provokes what we have said does not suffice, then cauterize until the blood is stopped.
And if these wounds are simple and small, then the cause of them is humidity; thus you should powder those areas with a powder, which consolidates and dries the area before the air can infect them.
And the method of the powder is this: take one part oil of anise, two parts resin of dragon, and three parts of unextinguished lime; let all be ground and crushed, and with it fill the wound, and constrain it with a good bandage until it adheres to the wound, and let it coagulate with the resin.
And then bind that dressing with bandages and leave it on, and do not remove it while it is like this so that it does not become infected, because the medicine is not eradicated from it until it is healed.
And sometimes make only a sole application, when you do not have anise and dragon resin at hand.
And perform this method of operation on large wounds when it is convenient that a dressing be placed over them and they be bound, and are recent wounds with their own resin, which the air has not yet altered.
And if the air has altered them, and especially in summer, then it is not suitable for the application of this powder, but rather cure them with what we have said, so that you apply on them certain digestive ointments, or you apply on them powders made from wheat flour mixed with water and honey until they form a paste; and then cure them with another remedy until they are healed.
Most likely the pain occurs at the fracture site in the bone, and it is small, then extract that with gestures.
And I will tell you about the treatment of head fractures in what is to be applied.
Of the sores of the neck.
Most likely if the sore occurs in the neck, then it is not different in medication, and between the sore of the head when it is simple.
Most likely if the nerve of the neck is cut or an artery, then if it is a nerve, it is not in the remedy but rather the treatment should be avoided with what causes vehement constriction, thus like cinchona and sage which are similar to veterinary and embalming treatments that harm the nerves and counteract that. And do not apply anything on the sore that causes excessive cold, because the substance of the nerves is fragile and their continuation is with the brain, which is the highest part of all the members.
And if it is treated with light medicines, such as a warm bath, some ointment rubbed in oil, either rose or not, and turpentine when washed with warm water and the other poultices prepared according to this manner, and anointed humidly.
If the wound is large, then administer a suture, or stitch the lips of it, and carefully cure that with powders until it is healed.
If the wound has depth or reaches to the lowest part of the body, then pierce that in the most depressed place.
If an artery has already been cut in the wound and a flow of blood is obtained, then separate or stop that, or tie it, or cauterize it if necessity demands it.
If the vertebrae of the throat or all have already been cut, and the veins of the neck are saved, then you adjust the lips of the wound with a suture on the cane of the throat and do not touch that; afterwards equalize that and return it to its natural figure, and place it with decent structure, and lift it for several days; and carefully cure it with plasters in which there is stripping and excitation until it is healed.

On the treatment of ulcers and fistulas.
Know that every wound and abscess that becomes inflamed and chronic, and becomes an ulcer, and is not consolidated and suppurates for a long time and is not resolved, however, in any member it may be, it is universally called fistula, and we call it azukem.
Fistula is truly a nodular, hard, white swelling for which there is no pain and to which there is a sensation similar to that of a pinched intestine; and thus the name for this type of swelling is called a "pinched" or "compressed" stone, that is to say, a kidney stone.
And it is in some men a moist tumor, which discharges urine; and for which the moisture is cut off in a few hours. And in some cases this moisture is moved, and it is little, and it is thick, and it is subtle.
It shows all those causes, and the signs of those and their cure with medicines in the division.
And it is necessary for you to know the cure of fistula, which is made by way of operation with the hand.
And know that fistulas occur in all the members of the body; for some of those are fistulas that reach the large veins and arteries, or the nerves, or the liver, or the intestine, or the bladder, or one of the ribs, or one of the vertebrae of the back, or one of the joints composed by composition like that of the hand and the foot; and of those which are close to the principal member and of similar things.
And therefore one of these fistulas that follows this manner is of the illnesses of difficult healing, and does not receive cure, and occupation with it is labor and ignorance.
